2801 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


North Shore Beach Property Owners Ass'n v. Brookhaven


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


115 N.Y.S.2d 670; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1734



September 2, 1952 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court were motions for temporary injunctions in four consolidated actions brought by petitioner members of a property owners' association to declare void and unconstitutional certain amendments to the Building Zone Ordinance of respondent Town of Brookhaven.


OVERVIEW: The court disregarded any defects in the notice of public hearings because the president of the property owners' association and about 30 individual owners appeared at the public hearing and gave both oral and written protests. There was no prejudice to the owners by any technical infirmity. With respect to the publication and posting of the amendments, a different situation arose. Under the ordinance in effect at the time the amendment was adopted, amendments to the zoning ordinance did not become effective until after it had been published in a newspaper, twice, and posted in six public places for not less than 10 days. Concededly, the amendments were only published once and posted in one place. The ordinance, Town of Brookhaven, N.Y., Law § 265, had since been amended to require only one publication and one posting; however, due to its effective date, the amendment did not serve to validate the action. Since the owners were only requesting a temporary injunction, it was not necessary to resolve the ultimate issues of fact. Enough was demonstrated to indicate a strong possibility that the owners would be successful to warrant temporarily maintaining the status quo.


OUTCOME: The court, in the exercise of its discretion, granted the motion for a temporary injunction in each case, provided the owner posted bond.

 

2802 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Central Westchester Humane Soc. v. Hilleboe


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Westchester County


202 Misc. 873; 115 N.Y.S.2d 769; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1750



August 30, 1952 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner medical society moved for permission to intervene in an action by plaintiffs, a humane society and others, against defendant Commissioner of Health of the State of New York. Plaintiffs sought a declaratory judgment that the Metcalf-Hatch Act, N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 5-a, was unconstitutional and they sought to enjoin the Commissioner from acting under and pursuant to § 5-a.


OVERVIEW: The society was the prime organization representing the interests of many hospitals, medical schools, research institutions, and laboratories in New York State in their interest in obtaining and use of animals for research purposes. The desperate shortage of research animals caused the society to strongly advocate the adoption of the Metcalf-Hatch Act, N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 5-a. The society sought to intervene in the action for declaratory judgment as a party defendant pursuant to N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act §§ 193, 193-b. Plaintiffs objected to the intervention of the society on the ground that it had no justiciable interest in the cause. The court granted intervention because the society, in its own right and as a representative of institutions sought to be benefited by the Act, was vitally interested in upholding the Act. The court noted that plaintiffs would not have been prejudiced by the intervention and that the action would not have been unduly delayed by the intervention. In fact, the court indicated that granting the motion might facilitate the final adjudication because of the society's long research and extensive knowledge of the facts that stimulated the enactment of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court grant the application for intervention.


HEADNOTES

Parties -- intervention -- action for judgment declaring that Public Health Law (§ 5-a), which permits use of stray animals for medical research, is unconstitutional; application of society for medical research, which assisted in sponsoring statute, for leave to intervene in action as party defendant granted under Civil Practice Act (§§ 193, 193-b).

In an action for a declaratory judgment that section 5-a of the Public Health Law, which permits the use of stray animals for medical research, is unconstitutional, the petition of a society for medical research, an organization which represented hospitals, schools, research institutions and laboratories in their efforts to obtain and use animals for research purposes and which assisted in drafting section 5-a and helped to influence its enactment, for leave to intervene as a party defendant, pursuant to sections 193 and 193-b of the Civil Practice Act, should be granted. Petitioner in its own right and as a representative of institutions benefiting by section 5-a is vitally interested in upholding the statute, and it is the rule that all persons who may [***2] be affected by a declaratory judgment should be joined as parties to an action for such judgment. Plaintiffs will not be prejudiced and the action will not be unduly delayed. Under section 193-b of the Civil Practice Act it is not required that a proposed intervener shall have a direct personal or pecuniary interest in the subject of the action. It is sufficient if he would be indirectly affected by the litigation in a substantial manner, and his claim or defense with respect to the subject matter of the litigation has a question of law or fact in common therewith.

 

2803 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Fleetwood Manor, Inc. v. Huntington Bay


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Suffolk County


115 N.Y.S.2d 615; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1722



August 29, 1952 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner filed an action against defendant Village of Huntington Bay, New York, seeking a declaration that the Zoning Ordinance of the Village of Huntington Bay was unconstitutional and void in as far as the landowner's property was concerned and to compel the Village to issue the landowner a certificate of occupancy for one family dwelling previously erected on the property.


OVERVIEW: A quarter acre of the landowner's property abutted the west side of a road. The property on the west side of the road was allowed to have one dwelling and appurtenances per one acre. The property on the east side of the road, nearest the landowner's quarter acre, was allowed to have one dwelling and appurtenances per quarter acre. The landowner's property was one and one quarter acres. The quarter acre was segregated from the one acre of property by a thirty-foot cliff. There was a dwelling on the quarter acre as well as on the one acre. The Village fined the landowner and the occupant of the dwelling on the quarter acre for violating the Ordinance. Upon review, the court determined that the Ordinance was invalid as to the landowner's property because the Ordinance permanently restricted the use of the landowner's property so as to constitute a taking without compensation. The court rejected the landowner's argument that the Ordinance on the whole was improperly adopted. The court concluded that the fine against the landowner and the occupant did not bind the court.


OUTCOME: The court declared the Ordinance invalid as to the landowner's property.

 

2804 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Tarrytown Road Restaurant, Inc. v. Hotel, Restaurant & Beverage Dispensers Union


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Westchester County


115 N.Y.S.2d 626; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1725; 22 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P67,124



August 18, 1952 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employer filed a motion for a temporary injunction against defendant union and its president to restrain them from picketing the employer's restaurant and interfering with its restaurant business. Defendants filed a cross-motion to dismiss the complaint for failure to allege compliance with N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act. § 876-a.


OVERVIEW: The employer discharged waitresses, who were members of the union. The employer filed a motion for a temporary injunction to restrain the union from picketing and interfering with its business. The union sought to dismiss the complaint. The trial court granted the employer's petition for injunction. The court denied the cross-motion to dismiss the complaint because the complaint upon its face set forth a good cause of action even thought it did not comply with the requirements of N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act § 876-a. The court held that because the union picketed with the objective of forcing an employer to recognize it as the bargaining agent and the representative of employees who did not choose the bargaining agent, § 876-a was not applicable. The court held that the employer was entitled to protection from disastrous and unfair economic pressure pending the determination of the action. The court found that § 876-a did not give license for the performance of unlawful or disorderly acts by a union. The court held that the union was temporarily restrained from all but peaceful and reasonable picketing on behalf of the claim of the discharged employees to reinstatement.


OUTCOME: The trial court granted the employer's petition for injunction to restrain the union from picketing and interfering with its business. The court denied the union's cross-motion to dismiss the complaint.

 

2805 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Harlem Slum Clearance Project


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court, Special Term, New York County, Part VIII


114 N.Y.S.2d 787; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1571



July 14, 1952 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner City of New York filed an application for an order to condemn certain real property under N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 72-k and for the compensation of each respective property owner.


OVERVIEW: The City filed an application for a condemnation order and for a determination as to the amount of compensation each property owner was to receive in accordance to a resolution that was adopted by the Board of Estimate. The property owners argued that the action and resolution of the Board was illegal because it did not have the authority to pass the resolution for the City's taking of the property for private purposes and not for public use. The court granted the City's application for an order of condemnation because under N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 72-k(1) the City was allowed to acquire real property that was necessary for or incidental to the clearance, re-planning, reconstruction, and neighborhood rehabilitation of substandard or unsanitary areas. In addition, under N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 72-k(2), the City was authorized to sell property that had been acquired for the purposes set forth in N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 72-k(1) in such as manner as prescribed by the Board. The proposed resale of the property for commercial purposes was incidental and ancillary to the primary purpose of the rehabilitation project and essential for the purpose sought to be accomplished by the City.


OUTCOME: The court granted the City's application for a condemnation order.

 

2806 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


O'Gara v. Joseph


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Kings County


202 Misc. 28; 115 N.Y.S.2d 469; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1696



July 9, 1952 



DISPOSITION: The plaintiff has failed to show that he has a case strong enough to warrant any temporary injunction and his motion is therefore denied. Submit order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff licensee sought a temporary injunction to enjoin defendant city officials during the pendency of the action from enforcing the tax on retail licensees of the State Liquor Authority imposed by New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code ch. 46, tit. F. The action was for a declaratory judgment and permanent injunction and asked that the city tax law be declared unconstitutional and void.


OVERVIEW: The licensee asked that the city tax law be declared unconstitutional and void. The licensee sought to enjoin the officials during the pendency of the action from enforcing the tax on retail liquor licensees. The court denied the injunction. The court held that the distinction for tax purposes between wholesale and retail dealers was previously upheld as not arbitrary. The court found that the law was not unreasonable, arbitrary, and discriminatory because the time of licensing was based upon the assumption that retail dealers in alcoholic beverages would have renewed their licenses from year to year. The court concluded that the law did not violate N.Y. Const. art. III, § 16 because the reference in the local law to the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law was merely to show the amount of the tax and to make the detailed description of retail licensees more explicit. The court rejected the licensee's argument that the liquor license constituted a contract with the State and that the imposition of the tax impaired the obligation of the contract because the licensee did not have a contract with the State but was merely granted a license or a temporary permit to sell alcoholic beverages.


OUTCOME: The court denied the licensee's request to enjoin the officials during the pendency of the action from enforcing the tax on retail liquor licensees.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- incorporation by reference -- taxation -- local tax on retail liquor sales -- (1) New York City local law imposing tax on retail liquor sales not arbitrary; claim that tax is less for some than for others overruled; tax of local law intended to apply for year but provision made for those in business for shorter time or whose liquor license not renewed -- (2) local law does not violate constitutional provision against incorporation by reference by fixing tax on basis of Alcoholic Beverage Control Law -- (3) liquor license is not contract; no obligation of contract impaired by tax -- (4) temporary injunction denied.

1. Local Law No. 58 of 1952 of the City of New York which imposes a tax on the privilege of selling liquor, wine or beer at retail for on or off premises consumption, is not unreasonable, arbitrary or discriminatory. The contentions that while the tax is imposed for a one-year period, plaintiff's license expires at the end of nine months of the [***2] tax year and that those who obtain their State license after March 1, 1952, will pay less tax for a full year than those who obtained their licenses prior to that date, are without merit. The local law is based upon the assumption that retail dealers in alcoholic beverages will renew their licenses from year to year and where the renewal occurs the licensee will be in business for the full tax year. Provision is also made in the local law for the exceptional cases where the license is not renewed during the tax year or where, for some other reason, the business ceases during the tax year. Those who enter business and obtain their licenses after the tax year begins to run will pay for the proportion of the tax year that they engage in business, except that a minimum tax will, in any event, have to be paid.

2. The local law does not violate section 16 of article III of the New York State Constitution which prohibits the incorporation of any existing law into another act by reference. The reference in the local law to the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law is merely to show the amount of the tax and to make the detailed description of retail licensees more explicit.

3. The argument [***3] that the liquor license constitutes a contract with the State and that the imposition of the tax impairs the obligation of this contract, is untenable. Plaintiff does not have a contract with the State but has been granted merely a license or a temporary permit to sell alcoholic beverages. Moreover, the rights granted by the issuance of the license to the plaintiff were accepted upon the terms and conditions which existed by reason of the provisions of chapter 278 of the Laws of 1947, as amended, which gave the city the right to impose the present tax.

4. Plaintiff has failed to make a sufficient showing to warrant a temporary injunction.

 

2807 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Stuyvesant Town Corp. v. Impellitteri


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


202 Misc. 661; 114 N.Y.S.2d 639; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2953



July 2, 1952 



DISPOSITION: Application granted to the extent indicated. Settle final order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a proceeding under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78, petitioner companies sought review of a determination by respondent Board of Estimate of the City of New York (board); sought to set aside that order; and sought an increase of the maximum average basic rental per month per room to an amount sufficient to provide sums for interest, amortization, and dividends under and pursuant to the terms of the parties' contract concerning a redevelopment project.


OVERVIEW: The court initially noted that as the parties' contract was upheld as valid in a previous case, the conclusion necessarily followed that the rights and obligations of the city as well as the city's board with respect to the contract and its terms were those stated and agreed upon therein. The court further noted that the statute provided that the contract was to regulate rentals, not the board. In addition, the board already had acknowledged the companies' right to a six percent return on their investment in the housing redevelopment project. The court then found that the equitable consideration of the interest and plight of the tenants, which motivated the board in denying the companies' application, did not justify or warrant the application's denial. Nevertheless, such equitable consideration did warrant the efforts made by the board to ameliorate the hardship and plight of the tenants in seeking fair adjustment by arriving at a reasonable compromise of the increase with respect to the present tenants. Accordingly, the court granted the companies' application for an increase, subject to the saving modification agreed to by the companies as to the present tenants.


OUTCOME: The court granted the companies' application for an increase in rental amounts, with the exception of the modification agreed to by the companies as to the present tenants of the housing redevelopment project.


HEADNOTES

Public housing -- redevelopment companies -- increase of rents -- (1) proceeding to require New York City board of estimate to grant application of housing development company and insurance company to increase rental per month per room in housing project to sum sufficient to provide 6% return on investment; petitioners entered into contract with city respecting construction and operation of project pursuant to Redevelopment Companies Law (L. 1942, ch. 845, as amd.); statute (§ 8) directs that contract shall regulate rents to be charged for rooms in project; contract provided for return to petitioner insurance company of 6% of final cost of project; in 1950 petitioner learned that final cost would be about $ 112,000,000 while earlier revised estimate had been $ 90,000,000 on which rent of $ 17 per month per room had been agreed upon by parties; board of estimate has refused petitioners' application that contract be amended by increasing average rental from $ 17 to $ 21 per month per room -- (2) purpose of Redevelopment Companies Law was rehabilitation,  [***2] with tenancy not restricted to "low-income" groups, "middle-income" groups or any other class of tenancy -- (3) contract of parties valid -- (4) provision embodying 6% return upon investment binding on parties -- (5) investment of petitioners is $ 112,210,057.64 which has been accepted as correct by board of estimate, and petitioners are entitled to return of 6% thereon -- (6) equitable consideration of tenants' interest which motivated board of estimate in denying petitioners' application did not justify such denial -- (7) proper action by board on application required grant to petitioners of increase of maximum average rental per month per room to sum sufficient to provide 6% return on investment; board should have granted petitioners' application with saving modification agreed to by petitioners of maximum average increase per month per room of $ 2.55 for three years and of $ 3 for fourth year in respect of present tenants -- (8) court, in proceeding under Civil Practice Act (art. 78), on proof presented may determine whether it will grant or withhold order, or direct modified relief.

1. In a proceeding under article 78 of the Civil Practice Act to annul a determination of the [***3] board of estimate of the City of New York and to require the board to grant the application of a housing redevelopment company and its parent company, an insurance company, to increase the maximum average basic rental per month per room in the housing project to an amount sufficient to provide sums for interest, amortization, and dividends under a contract between petitioners and the City of New York, it appears that petitioners entered into such contract with the city in 1943 respecting the acquisition of real property for, and the construction and operation of, the redevelopment project, pursuant to the Redevelopment Companies Law (L. 1942, ch. 845, as amd.). Such law authorizes the board of estimate to negotiate and approve contracts by which private capital may be provided for rehabilitation of substandard areas, the city is authorized to grant partial tax exemption to such projects, a limited return of 6% of the total actual final cost of the project is to be assured to the redevelopment company during the period of the partial tax exemption, and section 8 of the law directs that the contract shall regulate the rents to be charged for rooms in the project. The contract entered [***4] into between petitioners and the city provided for a return to petitioner insurance company during the period of the partial tax exemption of 6% of the final cost of the project. When the original agreement was entered into in 1943 the final cost was estimated at $ 60,000,000 and based thereon the contract provided a maximum average rental of $ 14 per month per room which was then believed sufficient to yield a 6% return on the estimated cost. Before the project was ready for occupancy it became apparent that the final cost would exceed $ 90,000,000, and therefore a supplemental agreement was entered into in 1947 to increase the maximum average rental from $ 14 to $ 17 per month per room. By the end of 1950 petitioners learned that the final cost of the project would be about $ 112,000,000. Petitioners thereupon applied to the board of estimate that the contract be amended by increasing the maximum average rental from $ 17 to $ 21 per month per room, but the board refused to grant the application.

2. The city contends that one of the purposes of the Redevelopment Companies Law was to encourage private investment in "middle-income" housing. The purpose of the law, however, was [***5] rehabilitation with tenancy not restricted to "low-income" groups, "middle-income" groups, or to any other class of tenancy.

3. The contract entered into between the parties is valid.

4. The provision embodying a 6% return upon the investment by petitioners in the project is valid and binding upon the parties.

5. The investment of petitioners is $ 112,210,057.64, which after audit by the city comptroller, has been accepted as correct by the board of estimate, and petitioners are entitled to a return of 6% on such investment.

6. Equitable consideration of the interest of the tenants which motivated the members of the board of estimate in denying petitioners' application did not justify such denial.

7. Proper action by the board of estimate on petitioners' application required a grant to petitioners of an increase of the maximum average rental per month per room to a sum sufficient to provide a 6% return on the investment. Petitioners offered to the board of estimate, immediately prior to the denial of their application by the board, to keep the rent increases per month per room to the present tenants at $ 2.55 for three years and at $ 3 for the fourth year. Had the board of estimate [***6] thereupon taken the action required as a matter of law, conserving as best it could under the circumstances the interests of the tenants, it would have granted petitioners' application with the saving modification agreed to by petitioners in respect of the present tenants.

8. The court, in a proceeding under article 78 of the Civil Practice Act, on the proof presented may determine whether, in the exercise of sound discretion, it will grant an order or withhold it or direct modified relief.

 

2808 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Peabody's Estate


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court, Special Term, New York County, Part III


115 N.Y.S.2d 337; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1674



July 2, 1952 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a proceeding by petitioner trustees for the judicial settlement of their trust account, the trustees sought an instruction as to whether the trust was liable to pay any portion of the federal tax payable by respondent estate.


OVERVIEW: The company set up an inter vivos trust in which it provided that the sole shareholder (the decedent) was to receive the income from the trust during his life. When decedent died, he was domiciled in Connecticut. His will was probated in that state. It was determined that the trust was part his estate for the purposes of federal estate taxation. At the time of the decedent's death, Connecticut had no statute dealing with the apportionment of estate taxes in the foreign jurisdiction, and therefore, the burden of the federal estate tax was on the residuary estate. Although later legislation was enacted that would have held the trust liable for estate taxes, Connecticut's highest court held that the statute could not be applied retroactively. Because that holding came from the highest court of the State that had adopted the law, the court was bound by it, and the trustees were not required to pay any portion of the federal estate tax; the decedent's estate was liable for the taxes. The court was not bound by a construction of the statute that was made by a federal court.


OUTCOME: The court held that the trustees were not required to pay any portion of the federal estate tax or any penalty or interest in connection therewith and did not need to make any contribution to the decedent's estate.

 

2809 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Papiernick v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


202 Misc. 717; 115 N.Y.S.2d 454; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1693



July 1, 1952 



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the plaintiff's motion for an injunction pendente lite is denied and the defendants' motion to dismiss the complaint is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers filed a complaint for an injunction pendente lite to restrain defendant city from collecting certain taxes on their vehicles. The city also filed a motion to dismiss the complaint that was filed by the taxpayers against the city.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers filed a complaint against the city to enjoin the city from collecting certain taxes on their vehicles. The tax measure was enacted pursuant to 1947 N.Y. Laws ch. 278, § 1, as amended by 1948 N.Y. Laws ch. 651. The taxpayers contended that the tax imposed on vehicles by the statute was invalid because it was in direct contravention of N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 54. The court held that where two statutes could be otherwise reconciled, the general statute had to yield to the specific statute, particularly where the specific statute was a later one. The court concluded that because there was a conflict between the two statutes, the specific grant of power in the 1947 statute prevailed over the local statute found in § 54. Finally, the court did not find that any unreasonable or unconstitutional classifications were created by the tax statutes at issue. The court denied the taxpayers' complaint for an injunction pendente lite and granted the city's motion to dismiss the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court rendered a judgment against the taxpayers on their complaint for an injunction pendente lite to restrain the city from collecting certain taxes on their vehicles. The court granted the city's motion to dismiss the complaint that was filed by the taxpayers against the city.


HEADNOTES

Motor vehicles -- tax on passenger vehicles by city -- constitutional law -- use tax on passenger vehicles -- (1) City of New York authorized (L. 1947, ch. 278, as amd.) to adopt local law imposing tax on use of passenger motor vehicles owned by residents of city; city, pursuant to such authority, enacted Local Law, No. 59 of 1952, imposing tax on use of motor vehicles upon streets of city; in action attacking local law on constitutional grounds, complaint should be dismissed -- (2) delegation of power to enact tax constitutional -- (3) Vehicle and Traffic Law (§ 54) prohibiting imposition of tax for use of public highways not violated by Local Law No. 59 since enabling act is specific, is later statute and supersedes general Vehicle and Traffic Law -- (4) local law not contrary to enabling act; failure of enabling act to use words indicating use of motor vehicle on "highways" or "streets" immaterial -- (5) tax not unreasonable  [***2] because applicable to residents and not nonresidents; normally, use of city streets by residents greater; classification is valid and constitutional.

1. By chapter 278 of the Laws of 1947 (as amd.), the Legislature authorized the City of New York to impose a tax "on the use of passenger motor vehicles * * * owned by residents". Pursuant to the authority thus conferred, Local Law No. 59 of the City of New York of 1952 was enacted and by its terms there was imposed a tax on any use of a motor vehicle owned by residents of the city upon the public streets of the city. In this action attacking said local law on constitutional grounds, the city's motion to dismiss the complaint should be granted.

2. The Legislature had constitutional and decisional authority to confer upon the city power to enact such tax.

3. Section 54 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law prohibits the imposition of local taxes for the use of public highways. Local Law No. 59 does not contravene section 54 since the enabling act (L. 1947, ch. 278) superseded the Vehicle and Traffic Law. The general statute, such as the Vehicle and Traffic Law, must yield to the specific statute which is a later one. That the Vehicle [***3] and Traffic Law has been amended from time to time after the enactment of chapter 278 is immaterial, for the amendments were inconsequential and there is nothing contained in that law which can be construed to supersede the specific provisions of chapter 278.

4. The enabling act authorized the imposition of a tax on the use of an automobile, but makes no reference to the use of an automobile upon the highway. The Legislature intended by the enabling act to signify the use of a passenger vehicle on the public highways of the city and the omission of the words "highways" or "streets" is of no moment.

5. Even if there is discrimination in the local law between residents and nonresidents, both of whom use the highways, the classification used in the local lawwas reasonable. Normally, the city's streets are used more frequently by residents than by nonresidents. That there may be occasional cases where a nonresident vehicle makes greater use of the city's streets than vehicles owned by residents is not determinative and is insufficient to justify a holding that the classification is unreasonable and thus unconstitutional.

 

2810 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


New York State Voters League against Vivisection, Inc. v. Hilleboe


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


202 Misc. 687; 114 N.Y.S.2d 805; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1574



June 30, 1952 



DISPOSITION: The motion is, therefore, in all respects denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs moved for a temporary injunction and attacked the validity of the Metcalf-Hatch Law (1952 N.Y. Law ch. 96).


OVERVIEW: The court stated that it was unnecessary to determine the question of whether or not either of plaintiffs would have been entitled to injunctive relief because the act, which was under attack was held to be constitutional. The court determined that the act authorized the state to requisition animals for scientific testing purposes and attempted to prevent cruelty to animals. The court found that N.Y. Penal Law § 185 (1947) permitted similar use of living animals in almost identical language. The court stated that reasonable regulations with respect to dogs and other animals was a valid exercise of the state's police power. There was no showing that the language of the act was broad enough to permit improper application or that any such application was threatened or contemplated. The court concluded that no rights of any person were affected by the requisitioning of animals in accordance with the provisions of the act and that the act was not in conflict with the state or federal constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court denied plaintiffs' request for a temporary injunction and held that the law was constitutional.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- animals -- use of animals in scientific tests -- statute (Public Health Law, § 5-a) authorizing use of living animals in scientific tests and experiments by authorized laboratories not unconstitutional; temporary injunction denied.

Chapter 96 of the Laws of 1952 (Public Health Law, § 5-a) authorizes the State Commissioner of Health to designate approved laboratories or institutions wherein scientific tests, experiments or investigations involving the use of living animals may be performed or conducted under prescribed rules, and provides that said commissioner or the commissioner of health of the City of New York may requisition, in lieu of destruction, unlicensed, unwanted or unclaimed animals impounded pursuant to law, at a fee to be fixed by the commissioner and paid by the laboratories. A motion for a temporary injunction is denied since the statute is not unconstitutional. Under State law there is only a qualified property in dogs and other animals. Reasonable regulations with respect to them constitute a valid exercise of the police power. Any expenditure [***2] of public funds required to implement the law is de minimis. The legislation otherwise in the public interest is not invalidated by the fact that some financial benefits may accrue to private institutions.

 

2811 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Linehan-Leary Corp. v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


202 Misc. 25; 115 N.Y.S.2d 466; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1695



June 30, 1952 



DISPOSITION: Since the court is not persuaded that Local Law No. 58 of 1952 is unconstitutional, the plaintiff is not entitled to an injunction, and the motion is accordingly denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff moved for a temporary injunction to restrain enforcement of the city tax on the privilege of selling liquor, wine, or beer at retail for on or off premises consumption, which was imposed by N.Y. Local Law 58 (1952).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sought to restrain enforcement of the local law because it allegedly violated N.Y. Const. art. III, § 16. The court found that the local law did not violate the provision because the reference in the local law to the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law merely fixed the amount of the tax, and it was not therefore required to be inserted into the local law itself. The court determined that the local law did not violate the home rule provisions of the State Constitution, the City Home Rule Law, or the City Charter because if the Control Law was ever amended, the city had the same power to amend the local law if it determined that a change was necessary. The city retained its full power to tax or not to tax for local purposes. The court found that the local law was clear and explicit. The court concluded that the allegation that the tax was an unlawful levy of an excise tax under N.Y. Const. art. XVI, § 3 was untenable. The court held that the local law was constitutional and denied plaintiff's motion for a temporary injunction.


OUTCOME: The court denied plaintiff's motion for an injunction.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- incorporation of law by reference -- taxation -- local tax on retail liquor sales -- (1) New York City local law imposing tax on retail liquor sales does not violate State Constitution (art. III, § 16) proscribing incorporation of existing law in statute by reference; reference to Alcoholic Beverage Control Law merely fixes amount of tax -- (2) home rule provisions not violated by local law -- (3) terms of local law explicit -- (4) claim that tax on New York County retailer more than on retailer in Richmond County and therefore discriminatory overruled -- (5) no contract obligation impaired by local law -- (6) tax is not unlawful levy of excise tax -- (7) local law constitutional and temporary injunction against tax denied.

1. Local Law No. 58 of 1952 of the City of New York which imposes a tax on the privilege of selling liquor, wine or beer, at retail for on or off premises consumption does not violate section 16 of article III of the State [***2] Constitution which proscribes incorporating an existing law in a statute except by inserting it therein. The reference in the local law to the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law merely fixes the amount of the tax, thereby informing the taxpayer that it must pay 25% of the license fee it paid under the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law for the license issued to it, and without which it would neither be in business nor liable for the city tax.

2. The contention that the local law violates the home rule provisions of the State Constitution, the City Home Rule Law and the New York City Charter, based on the reasoning that the State Legislature may amend the Alcoholic Beverage Control Law and would thereby amend the city local law either by increasing or decreasing the amount of tax imposed, or by abolishing it altogether, is overruled. Should this occur, the city council is likewise free to amend its law, if it so determines. There is no infringement of any home rule provisions. The city retains full power to tax or not to tax for local purposes. It is given its power to levy this tax by the enabling act.

3. The terms of the local law are sufficiently explicit to inform those who are subject [***3] to it as to what conduct on their part will render them liable to any penalty.

4. A claim that the tax discriminates against plaintiff -- based on the fact that the State license fee in New York County is $ 1,200, and only $ 800 in Richmond County, so that under the local law plaintiff, who is in New York County, pays a city tax of $ 300 and a tavern in Richmond County pays a city tax of $ 200 -- is overruled. Such a classification is valid.

5. A claim that the local law impairs the obligation of a contract between the State and its licensee arising out of the issuance of such license, even though the license cannot be revoked except for cause, is without merit.

6. A claim that the tax is an unlawful levy of an excise tax under section 3 of article XVI of the State Constitution is untenable. This tax is an excise tax on the privilege of selling liquor, wine or beer at retail for on or off premises consumption, and not an ad valorem tax on the license nor an excise tax levied solely because of the ownership of intangible personal property. Nor is it a tax on income or gross receipts, neither of which is a factor in determining the amount of tax.

7. Since Local Law No. 58 of 1952 [***4] is constitutional, plaintiff is not entitled to a temporary injunction.

 

2812 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


New York v. Bevevino


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Magistrate's Court of New York, Borough of Manhattan, Municipal Term Court


202 Misc. 723; 112 N.Y.S.2d 647; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2680



May 7, 1952 



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the motion to dismiss the complaint is denied. The defendant may plead or stand trial, as required by section 330 of the Code of Criminal Procedure.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss, pursuant to N.Y. Code. Crim. Proc. § 330, the State's complaint that charged defendant with having unlawfully caused, suffered, and allowed dense smoke to be discharged from a stationary boiler, a violation of paragraph 1.1.1 of subdivision 1.1 of rule 1 of the Rules and Regulations of the Bureau of Smoke Control.


OVERVIEW: In support of his motion to dismiss, defendant argued that the Council of the City of New York, by enacting New York City, N.Y. Local Law 5 (1949), did not declare the emission of dense smoke to be a violation of law, but delegated to the bureau of smoke control the power to enact laws declaring what constituted a violation of law. According to defendant, the council unconstitutionally delegated its legislative function to an administrative body. Defendant further argued that only the bureau's rules and regulations declared the emission of dense smoke a violation of law, and thus constituted an attempt to exercise a nondelegable legislative power. The court held that the New York City, N.Y Admin. Code § D26-1.0 provided for the adoption of rules and regulations by the board under its mandate and declared the punishment for violations. Therefore, the court held that the rule prohibiting dense smoke was issued by the board of smoke control pursuant to the constitutional command of the council and that it was a valid and substantive offense by enactment of the New York City, N.Y. Local Law No. 5 (1949), New York City, N.Y. Admin. Code § D26-1.0.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- smoke control -- New York City council by Local Laws, 1949, No. 5 created board of smoke control, provided for control of smoke, and established penalties for violation of rules of board; no unconstitutional delegation of power to board of smoke control given; local law provides penalties for violation of rules of board of smoke control; board of smoke control has established regulations; regulations presumed reasonable; council, not board, has enacted law; in prosecution against defendant for emitting dense smoke, motion to dismiss complaint denied.

Local Law No. 5 of 1949 of the City of New York deals with smoke control, provides for the creation of a bureau of smoke control, and a board of smoke control, and declares violation of the rules of the board of smoke control to be punishable by fine or imprisonment or both. The city council itself has enacted the offense and thereby exercised the substantive law-making power. The substantive portion [***2] of the legislation is found in that part of the statute which declares the violation of the rules and regulations to be a crime and prescribes the punishment for such violation. The rules and regulations adopted by the board of smoke control, pursuant to statutory direction, constitute a comprehensive scheme of regulation and control of air pollution. There is a presumption of the existence of facts establishing that these rules and regulations represent a reasonable exercise of the police power. Accordingly, the rule prohibiting dense smoke was issued by the board pursuant to the constitutional command of the council, and it is a valid and substantive offense by enactment of said local law. Accordingly, there has been no unlawful delegation by the council of the City of New York to the board of smoke control of power to enact laws. In this prosecution against defendant for allowing dense smoke to be discharged from a stationary boiler used with a hoisting crane, defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint should be denied.

 

2813 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Sunshine Book Co. v. McCaffrey


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


8 Misc. 2d 327; 112 N.Y.S.2d 476; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1547



April 25, 1952 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The motion is in all respects denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff publisher brought action for a declaratory judgment and for a permanent injunction against defendant Commissioners of Police and of Licenses of the City of New York. The publisher moved for an injunction pendente lite to preventive police from arresting newsstand employees for selling obscene material.


OVERVIEW: The publisher put out a magazine who's subject matter was ostensible the nudist culture. While it contained many pictures that showed nudists engaged in athletic activities, it also contained many pictures that showed frontal nude pictures of women in provocative position the magazine as well as on the cover each month. The commissioner of licenses issued a notice telling newsdealers that their licenses would be revoked if continued to sell the publisher's magazine. Subsequently, many newsstand operators were arrested for selling the publisher's magazine. The publisher brought an action for an injunction and challenged the constitutionality of N.Y. Penal Law § 1141(1). The court found that the statute was constitutional as the definition of obscenity could be determined by community standards. It further held that the dominant purpose of the photographs was to attract the attention of the public by an appeal to their sexual impulse; thus, the arrests were proper. Additionally, the notice released by the Commissioner of Licenses did not constitute a prior restraint within the constitutional prohibition.


OUTCOME: The motion was in all respects denied.


HEADNOTES

Injunctions -- obscenity -- in action to restrain New York City Commissioner of Licenses from threatening licensed newsdealers with suspension or revocation of licenses if they displayed or sold nudist sunbathing periodicals, plaintiffs' motion for injunction pendente lite denied. (Penal Law, § 1141, subd. 1; New York City Charter, §§ 773, 885; Administrative Code of City of New York, § B32-58.0 to B32-74.1; N. Y. Const., art. I, § 8; U. S. Const., 1st and 14th Amdts.)

The Penal Law (§ 1141, subd. 1) prohibits the sale or distribution of "any obscene, lewd, lascivious, filthy, indecent or disgusting book, magazine, pamphlet, newspaper * * * photograph" etc. The Commissioner of Licenses of the City of New York has regulatory power over sidewalk newsstands (New York City Charter, §§ 773, 885; Administrative Code of City of New York, § B32-58.0 to B32-74.1). The commissioner warned all such newsdealers, under penalty of suspension or revocation of their licenses, not to display or sell two periodicals published by two nudist sunbathing, nonprofit New Jersey corporations. Those magazines contain photographs glorifying nudism,  [***2] and their covers always contain such photographs. The magazines are for sale to all persons, regardless of sex or youth. The warning by the commissioner was not an unconstitutional prior restraint upon publication (N. Y. Const., art. I, § 8; U. S. Const., 1st and 14th Amdts.). The warning was generally understood as limited to issues of those magazines containing nude photographs. Perhaps the commissioner should amend his warning to state so definitely. But, in this action by the nudist corporations and by their New York distributing corporation for an injunction against the commissioner, and also against the commissioner of police who has arrested four newsdealers, plaintiff's motion for an injunction pendente lite is denied.

 

2814 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Playtown Products, Inc. v. Ideal Toy Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Trial Term, New York County


201 Misc. 911; 113 N.Y.S.2d 102; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2748



April 18, 1952 



DISPOSITION: Motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation filed a motion to vacate a directed verdict in favor of defendant corporation in plaintiff's action for breach of contract.


OVERVIEW: The issue on trial was whether plaintiff was hired to design toys for defendant or whether plaintiff's activities were an effort to sell a line of toys to defendant. Plaintiff testified to facts that, if believed, would make out a prima facie case, but the weight of the credible testimony was against it. The jury rendered a verdict for plaintiff. On motion, that verdict was set aside and a motion for direction for defendant granted. Plaintiff argued that the motion directing the verdict exceeded the powers of the court because in the state of proof a verdict could not be directed at any time. N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act § 457-a provided that the court could direct a verdict when it would be required to set aside a contrary verdict for legal insufficiency of evidence. The court found that the words "legal insufficiency of evidence" included insufficient evidence to sustain the burden of proof. Where the evidence was sufficient to go to the jury, a verdict could not be directed. The evidence was insufficient to go to the jury if there was none that ought reasonably to satisfy a jury that the fact sought to be proved was established. Under that test the verdict was properly directed.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion.


HEADNOTES

Trial -- direction of verdict -- (1) plaintiff had established facts which, if believed, would make out prima facie case, but weight of credible testimony was against plaintiff; after jury rendered verdict for plaintiff, verdict set aside and defendant's motion for directed verdict granted; since evidence of plaintiff not reasonably sufficient to satisfy jury, granting of motion for directed verdict proper under Civil Practice Act (§ 457-a) -- (2) while directed verdict inconsistent with denial of motion to dismiss complaint, section 457-a permits directed verdict in such circumstances.

1. Plaintiff at a trial had testified to facts which, if believed, would make out a prima facie case, but the weight of the credible testimony was against plaintiff. A motion to dismiss the complaint was denied and decision on defendant's motion for a directed verdict was reserved. The jury rendered a verdict for plaintiff. On motion, the verdict for plaintiff was set aside and the motion for a directed verdict in favor of defendant was granted. Under section 457-a of the Civil Practice Act which provides that the court may direct [***2] a verdict "when it would be required to set aside a contrary verdict for legal insufficiency of evidence", a verdict may be directed where there is evidence to go to a jury but such evidence is not sufficient reasonably to satisfy a jury that the fact sought to be proved is established. Under this test a verdict was properly directed for defendant.

2. While such a ruling is theoretically inconsistent with a denial of a motion to dismiss the complaint, it is expressly permitted by section 457-a.

 

2815 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Black River Regulating Dist. v. Adirondack League Club


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Oneida County


201 Misc. 808; 115 N.Y.S.2d 572; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1715



March 24, 1952 



DISPOSITION: The defendant is entitled to an order dismissing the complaint and granting summary judgment. The remaining motions are dismissed as they are now academic. Submit order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant club filed a motion for summary judgment to dismiss the declaratory judgment action brought by plaintiffs, regulating district and others (district). The primary motion made by the club asked for judgment for the club on the pleadings pursuant to N.Y. R. Civ. Prac. 112 or, in the alternative, an order pursuant to N.Y. R. Civ. Prac. 113 dismissing the complaint and for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The district sought a judgment declaring that it was entitled to maintain condemnation proceedings against the club to acquire lands owned by it that were needed to construct a reservoir. The district also sought a declaration that the Stokes Act was invalid and unconstitutional in so far as it prevented the district's board from constructing the reservoir. The court granted the club's motion. The court determined that the complaint alleged the making of the determination and final order of the district's board after the required public hearing, but the evidence proved that the order had subsequently become null and void after the petition was dismissed at the direction of the appellate court, and no further determination and final order as provided for in N.Y. Conserv. Law § 453 was alleged. Thus, the court ruled that the plan for the construction of a reservoir no longer existed and the district was not entitled to maintain condemnation proceedings against the club to acquire lands owned by it for construction of the reservoir. Nor was it entitled to an advisory opinion on the constitutionality of the Stokes Act given that no justiciable issue was presented.


OUTCOME: The court granted the club's motion for summary judgment dismissing the district's complaint for declaratory judgment and other relief.


HEADNOTES

Waters and watercourses -- construction of reservoir by river regulating district -- (1) action by river regulating district for declaration that it can maintain condemnation proceedings against defendant to acquire lands for construction of reservoir; plaintiff pursuant to Conservation Law adopted and determined plan for construction of reservoir on river and defendant brought proceeding to review such determination; determination was confirmed by Appellate Division; 1950 Legislature then amended Conservation Law (§ 445) to provide that no reservoir could be constructed on Moose River by any river regulating board; on appeal, Court of Appeals reversed Appellate Division and held that 1950 amendment disposed of plaintiff board's plan and directed dismissal of proceeding to review on ground that issues moot; result therefore that final plan of board for construction of reservoir no longer in existence and plaintiff  [***2] is not entitled to maintain condemnation proceedings against defendant to acquire lands for construction of reservoir -- (2) plaintiff not entitled to prosecute action for purpose of obtaining opinion as to constitutionality of amendment of Conservation Law (§ 445) -- (3) individual plaintiffs lack legal capacity to test constitutionality of amendment -- (4) since defense established by documentary evidence, defendants entitled to summary judgment dismissing complaint.

1. In an action by plaintiff, Black River Regulating District, for a declaration that it is entitled to acquire lands owned by defendant and necessary for construction of a reservoir to control the flow of water on the Moose River, it appeared that plaintiff had, pursuant to statute (Conservation Law, art. VII-A, now art. VII), prepared a plan for the development of a reservoir on the Moos e River and that the determination of the board to construct the reservoir was made after a required public hearing. Thereafter defendant brought a proceeding to review such determination and the determination was confirmed by the Appellate Division, Fourth Department ( Matter of Adirondack League Club v. Board of Black  [***3] Riv. Regulating Dist., 275 App. Div. 618, 92 N.Y.S.2d 256). The 1950 Legislature, however, amended section 445 of the Conservation Law to provide that no reservoir, except for municipal water supply, should be constructed in Hamilton or Herkimer Counties on the Moose River by any river regulating board. Upon appeal to the Court of Appeals from the confirmation by the Appellate Division, the Court of Appeals reversed such confirmation, and ruled that the 1950 amendment had completely disposed of plaintiffs' plan and directed dismissal of the proceeding to review on the ground that the issues were moot (301 N. Y. 219, 93 N.E.2d 647). Accordingly, when the petition to review the final determination of the board was dismissed by Special Term as directed by the remittitur of the Court of Appeals, the final plan of the board directing the construction of the reservoir was disposed of by implication of law as well as the language of the court. The contention that the amendment of the Conservation Law (§ 445) is unconstitutional and that in a condemnation proceeding to be instituted by plaintiff, defendant could raise all questions as to the necessity and validity of the proposed taking,  [***4] is rejected, for defendant would be deprived of an opportunity to have the Court of Appeals pass upon the questions raised by it in the proceeding to review the final order of the board as provided in section 454 of the Conservation Law and article 78 of the Civil Practice Act. When a statutory right is given a party affected by the final determination of a board, the court may not deprive the party of such a right. The documentary evidence and official records conclusively prove that the determination of plaintiff board became null and void upon dismissal of the proceeding to review pursuant to the direction of the Court of Appeals and in contemplation of law no plan for the construction of a reservoir on the Moose River now exists and plaintiff is not entitled to maintain condemnation proceedings against defendant to acquire lands for construction of a reservoir.

2. Accordingly, plaintiff may not prosecute this action for the purpose of obtaining an advisory opinion as to the constitutionality of the amendment of section 445 of the Conservation Law, for there is no justiciable issue presented.

3. The individual plaintiffs have no legal capacity to test the constitutionality of [***5] the amendment.

4. Since the documentary evidence and official records prima facie establish defendant's defense and plaintiffs have failed by affidavit or other proof to impugn said documentary evidence and official record, defendant is entitled to summary judgment dismissing the complaint in this action for a declaratory judgment.

 

2816 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


L. X. Corp. v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


201 Misc. 400; 115 N.Y.S.2d 120; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1624



March 14, 1952 



DISPOSITION: The motion to dismiss the complaint is accordingly granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner brought an action against defendant city contesting the sewer rent charged by the city as a tax.


OVERVIEW: The property owner contested the city's sewer rent as a tax in violation of N.Y. Const. art VIII, § 10. The court noted that the sewer was fixed at one third of the water charges assessed in respect of the property owner's dwelling. Although those water charges were actually fixed on a frontage rate instead of by actual metering, neither the water charge or the sewer rent was fixed without regard to the quantity of water used or of the use made of the sewer. The court concluded that the sewer rent was a charge for the special benefit conferred upon those who used the sewer system and hence was not a tax.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the property owner's complaint.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- sewer rent -- (1) complaint in action by owner of multiple dwelling to recover sewer rent on claim that sewer rent is tax and together with real estate tax exceeds constitutional 2% tax limit of assessed valuation, should be dismissed -- (2) sewer rent is charge for special benefit conferred upon those using sewer system and is not tax.

1. New York City Local Laws (1950, Nos. 67 and 102) imposed a sewer rent on plaintiff, as owner of a multiple dwelling connected with the city's sewer system. An action to recover a sewer rent paid under protest, on the contention that the sewer rent is a tax and that the sewer rent and the regular real estate tax together exceed the constitutional tax limitation of 2% upon assessed valuation should be dismissed.

2. The sewer rent here complained of is fixed at one third of the water charges assessed in respect of plaintiff's dwelling. Neither the water charge nor the sewer rent is fixed without regard to the quantity of water used or the use made of the sewer. Accordingly, the sewer rent is a charge [***2] for the special benefit conferred upon those who use the sewer system and hence is not a tax.

 

2817 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Civil Service Employees Ass'n v. Hurd


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Rensselaer County


202 Misc. 386; 112 N.Y.S.2d 721; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2686



March 10, 1952 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a civil service employee individually and on behalf of other similarly situated employees and a civil service employees membership corporation, instituted a proceeding under N.Y. Civ. Prac. Act art. 78 to compel respondent Director of the Budget of the State of New York to approve a determination reallocating the employee's salary position. The Director filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The Director claimed that his action in disapproving another administrative official's reallocation of the employee's position from grade G-8 to grade G-9 was not judicially reviewable and that petitioners failed to plead facts raising any issue as to the propriety of the Director's action. Noting that there was nothing in the New York Civil Service Law or any other law that exempted the Director's acts from review, the court declined to determine whether it was prohibited from substituting its judgment for the Director's until it had the benefit of the Director's answer. As to the sufficiency of the petition, the court determined that the employee alleged facts that, taken as true, entitled the employee prima facie to the relief he requested and ordered the Director to answer the petition. The court further determined that all of the questions could be determined and full relief accorded to the employee and others similarly situated without the corporation's intervention. The court concluded that there was no reason to permit the corporation to participate in the proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court denied the Director's motion to dismiss as to the employee and granted the motion as to the corporation.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- reclassification -- review of denial of reclassification -- (1) action of State Budget Director in denying approval of change of grade of civil service employee subject to review if arbitrary; question can be determined only after answer to petition to review filed; proceeding not dismissed where Budget Director claimed his action not reviewable -- (2) petition sufficient in law since allegations of fact show that denial arbitrary -- (3) membership corporation of civil service employees improperly joined as petitioner and proceeding dismissed as to it, where all questions may be determined without association's intervention.

1. The State Director of Classification and Compensation changed the grade of a civil service employee upwards. The State Budget Director disapproved of the determination relying on subdivision 1 of section 39-a of the Civil Service Law, which provides that a change of grade shall become effective on the first day of the fiscal year following approval by the Budget Director. A denial of approval by the Budget Director may be reviewed if arbitrary or capricious.  [***2] The Budget Director may not obtain dismissal of a proceeding to review such determination before answer on the ground that his action is not reviewable. Only by the answer to the petition can it be determined that his action was not arbitrary.

2. The petition alleges that the action of the Budget Director was arbitrary and that the facts found by the Director of the Classification and Compensation Division required the allocation of the position to a higher grade. Since these allegations are deemed admitted on a motion to dismiss a petition for insufficiency in law, the motion should be denied. The petition states facts upon which petitioner is entitled prima facie to the relief sought.

3. A membership corporation of civil service employees has improperly been joined as a party petitioner. The individual petitioner sues on behalf of himself and all others similarly situated. All of the questions may be determined and full relief accorded to all those affected without the association's intervention. The motion to dismiss the petition as to the corporate petitioner should be granted.

 

2818 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Oswald v. Christy


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court, Special Term, New York County, Part III


112 N.Y.S.2d 913; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2721



March 5, 1952 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant initiated prosecution of plaintiff property owner for violating New York City, N.Y., R. 1(1.1), governing emissions from a smokestack. The property owner then brought the declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of Rule 1(1.1) and defendant filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings to dismiss the complaint for insufficiency. The property owners filed a cross-motion to strike the defenses.


OVERVIEW: The property owner operated a smokestack that emitted smoke into the atmosphere. After defendant charged the property owner with violating Rule 1(1.1), the property owner challenged the constitutionality of that Rule. The property owner claimed that the Rule improperly interfered with property ownership rights. The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the declaratory judgment action, finding that the patent importance and the propriety of full inquiry and investigation in the cause warranted the retention of jurisdiction. The court also found that the Rule seemed to fall within the objective outlined in New York City, N.Y., Local Law No. 5 (1949) for the regulation and control of emissions. With regard to defendant's defenses, the court held that the claims that adoption of the Rule was a proper exercise of administrative function, that defendant was a proper party, and that the Rule was valid and reasonable were sufficient to withstand challenge. However, the court dismissed the defense of adequacy of remedy at law, finding that the declaratory judgment avenue for relief was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion and denied the cross-motion, except to the extent that it was granted to strike out a defense regarding the adequacy of a remedy at law.

 

2819 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Lincoln Rochester Trust Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Surrogate's Court of New York, Monroe County


201 Misc. 1008; 111 N.Y.S.2d 45; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2477



February 27, 1952 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner trustee initiated judicial settlement of account proceedings that concerned a discretionary common trust fund account that was established pursuant to N.Y. Banking Law § 100(c). Respondent special guardians objected to the constitutionality of § 100(c) and the plan of operations that was filed by the trustee.


OVERVIEW: The special guardians objected to the constitutionality of § 100(c) under which the common trust fund was created. The court dismissed the objections that were filed by the special guardians because § 100(c) did not violate due process by failing to provide notice to infants and incompetents of the intention to invest moneys of prospective participating trusts in the common trust fund. The fact that § 100(c) authorized a trustee to commingle trust funds without notice to the beneficiaries did not pertain to the constitutionality of § 100(c) because in most cases infants and incompetents would have been unable to come forward after they had received the notices anyway. Section 100(c) did not permit self-dealing because N.Y. Banking Law § 100(c)(4) required that the trust company's fund assets were kept separately from the trust company's own assets. Section 100(c) was not discriminatory when it authorized only corporate trustees to create common trust funds because § 100(c) applied equally to all corporations that were known to handle multiple trusts.


OUTCOME: The court submitted a decree that dismissed the objections that were filed by the special guardians and approved the common fund trust account as filed by the trustee.


HEADNOTES

Banks and banking -- common trust funds -- (1) that Banking Law (§ 100-c, subd. 9) authorizes corporate trustee of common trust fund to commingle trust funds without notice to infants, incompetents and unknowns, does not go to its constitutionality, but relates to policy -- (2) similarly, subdivisions 8 and 10 of section 100-c which permit self-dealing by trustee involve matter of policy -- (3) failure of statute to require "documentary" evidence of investments constitutes regulatory matter only and does not render statute unconstitutional -- (4) provision for period of time between decision to withdraw funds and time of actual withdrawal deprives no one of substantive rights -- (5) same is true as to provision for triennial accountings -- (6) statute is valid in limiting cotrustee's investment discretion to deciding whether or not to withdraw underlying trust assets from common trust fund -- (7) statute not discriminatory where, although it does not apply to all persons, it applies equally to all persons (corporations)  [***2] handling multiple trusts -- (8) objection that statute discriminatory may not be made in this proceeding where no individual trustee claimed to be discriminated against is party hereto -- (9) statute not unconstitutional insofar as it authorizes funds of trusts created before enactment of statute to be invested in common trust funds -- (10) participating shares in common trust fund constitute "securities" in which funds of trust may be invested -- (11) Surrogate's Court has jurisdiction of judicial settlements of common trust funds containing inter vivos trust funds -- (12) other objections relate to reasonableness of plan of operation under statute rather than to its legality; but provision in plan that cost of audit of common trust fund shall be chargeable to principal thereof relates to management costs which may not be charged against such fund (subd. 4) -- (13) affidavit of mailing of notices which incorporates by reference names and addresses appearing on filed list is regular -- (14) statute does not require as to said list statement of nature of interests of named persons -- (15) that name "Hardenbrook" was erroneously spelled as "Hardenbreek" in list does not make publication  [***3] defective -- (16) permission of State Banking Board for establishment of fund, and authorizations of Federal Reserve System and of State Banking Board permitting $ 50,000 investments, not required to be filed -- (17) objection that investment by participating trust now exceeds $ 50,000 value has become academic; amended subdivision 1 has increased limitation of investments to $ 100,000 -- (18) objections that under underlying wills more than one trust was created in amounts less than $ 50,000 but which aggregated more than $ 50,000, and that remainders of trusts may cause assets to be held later for one beneficiary, untenable; "presently payable" test approved -- (19) trustee was authorized to use nominee in its security transactions -- (20) filed list shows that notices of judicial settlement were mailed directly to beneficiaries -- (21) where trustee does not seek adjudication as to its right under underlying instruments to make investments in common trust fund and no decree entered thereon, beneficiaries not barred from raising such questions in judicial settlement proceedings in underlying trusts.

1. That subdivision 9 of section 100-c of the Banking Law authorizes the trustee [***4] of a common trust fund to commingle underlying trust funds in a common trust fund without notice to infants, incompetents and to persons whose names and addresses have not come to the knowledge of trustee does not go to the constitutionality of the statute, but goes to a matter of policy of the State.

2. Similarly, the objectant's claim in this accounting proceeding by petitioner corporation, as trustee of a common trust fund, that subdivisions 8 and 10 of section 100-c permit self-dealing by the trustee goes largely to a matter of policy, and not of constitutionality. Such claim, however, is unfounded in view of subdivision 4 of the statute and judicial construction of the subdivision to the effect that the trustee must keep assets of fund separate from its own, and in its fiduciary capacity may not deal with itself or any affiliate.

3. The failure of the statute to require so-called "documentary" evidence of investments and transfers and of other notices thereof may affect the opportunity for self-dealing, but does not amount to authorization thereof. This is a regulatory matter only, and does not render the statute unconstitutional.

4. The statutory provision for a stated period [***5] of time between a decision to withdraw funds from the common trust fund and the time of actual withdrawal is for the protection of the beneficiaries and deprives no one of substantive rights. It is proper, regulatory legislation.

5. The same is true with respect to the statutory provisions for triennial accountings.

6. Subdivision 1 of section 100-c requires the consent of the cotrustee to the investment of funds of the underlying trust into a common trust fund. However, the cotrustee's investment discretion in respect to the shares in the common trust fund evidencing the participation of the underlying trust assets is limited to deciding whether or not to withdraw such assets (subd. 5). Although this is a departure from previous trust practice, changing times have indicated the need and wisdom thereof, and none can question the power of the Legislature to make a change.

7. Nor can it be said that the statute is unconstitutional as discriminatory because it authorizes only corporate trustees to create common trust funds, inasmuch as it does apply equally to all persons (corporations) known to be handling multiple trusts, wherein lie problems sought to be solved in part by the [***6] legislation.

8. Nor may such objection properly be made in this proceeding since no individual trustee against whom the statute is claimed to discriminate is a party to this proceeding and objecting herein, and neither of the two special guardians herein represents any such trustee.

9. Nor is the statute unconstitutional insofar as it authorizes funds of trusts created before the enactment of the statute to be invested in common trust funds, on the claimed ground that it authorizes impairment of contracts. What constitutes proper investments for trust funds is determined by the law in effect when the investment is made.

10. The participating shares in a common trust fund constitute "securities" in which funds of a trust may be invested.

11. The Surrogate's Court has jurisdiction over judicial settlement proceedings of common trust funds which contain inter vivos trust funds.

12. Other objections relate to the reasonableness of plan of operation under statute, rather than to its legality. The Banking Board had power to permit the accounting trustee to establish the present fund with provisions for its operation as stated in the filed plan. However, the provision in the filed [***7] plan that the cost of an audit of the common trust fund shall be chargeable against, and payable out of, the principal of such common trust fund contravenes the statute, for it relates, not to a judicial settlement proceeding, but to management costs, and such costs, under subdivision 4 of section 100-c of the Banking Law, may not be charged against a common trust fund by a trust company.

13. The affidavit of mailing of notices which incorporates by reference names and addresses appearing on the list which was required to be filed by subdivision 12 of section 100-c and was in fact duly filed herein, is regular.

14. The statute does not require, in respect to said list, a statement of the nature of interests of persons named and classification of paragraph (1) of subdivision 12 in which they fall.

15. Where, due to a printer's error, the name "Hardenbrook" was misspelled as "Hardenbreek" in said list, does not make the publication defective, particularly since in the same clause the same family name is correctly printed.

16. There was no requirement that the permission of the State Banking Board to the trustee to establish the fund and the authorization of the Federal Reserve System [***8] and of the Banking Board permitting investments in the sum of $ 50,000 be filed.

17. The objection to the trustee's conduct of the fund in that, although the original investment by the participating trust was in the sum of $ 49,968.78, at the date of the account, the investment exceeds the value of $ 50,000, has become academic, since the amendment (L. 1951, ch. 215) of subdivision 1 of section 100-c has increased the limitation on participations to the sum of $ 100,000. Nevertheless, a fair interpretation of the provision must fix the time of valuation at the date of the investment, and not require withdrawal in whole or in part solely by reason of a mere increment in capital value.

18. Further objections involve underlying wills under which in each case more than one trust was created in amounts less than $ 50,000, but which aggregated more than $ 50,000 and all of such trusts have participated in the common trust fund. That the remainders of the trust may cause the assets later to be held for one beneficiary is immaterial, since the "presently payable" test has been adopted by the Banking Board and is judicially approved.

19. A common trust fund constitutes an express trust [***9] within the meaning of section 25 of the Personal Property Law, and the trustee was authorized to use a nominee in its security transactions (Surrogate's Ct. Act, § 231).

20. The list filed herein pursuant to subdivision 12 of the statute shows that the notices of judicial settlement were mailed directly to the beneficiaries, and not to the beneficiaries of the trust in care of the petitioning trustee as contended by the objectants.

21. The accounting trustee made no attempt in its petition or account to show particular authority in each instrument creating the participating trusts under which the investment in the common trust fund was made and said trustee does not seek an adjudication as to its right under those instruments to make such investments. If the decree entered herein is also silent on that issue, the beneficiaries on accountings in the underlying trusts will not be barred from having such issue determined. Insofar as such questions are raised and determined in this proceeding, the adjudication here will be conclusive on all parties (Banking Law, § 100-c, subd. 14); and the court determines in its discretion that under the statute it was proper for such questions [***10] to be raised herein.

 

2820 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Mid-States Freight Lines, Inc. v. Bates


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Ulster County


200 Misc. 885; 111 N.Y.S.2d 568; 1952 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2545



January 23, 1952 



DISPOSITION: The motion of the plaintiffs for a temporary injunction is denied. The motion of the defendants for judgment on the pleadings is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:
