Sections 134 and 135 of the [***2] Public Housing Law provide that in a proceeding, such as this, by a limited dividend housing company to condemn a parcel of real property for low-rent housing for persons of low income, the certificate issued by the State Housing Commissioner shall be "conclusive evidence" that the acquisition of the property is necessary for the construction of a low-rent housing project and that the acquisition is in the public interest and necessary for the public use. It may be assumed that the Legislature cannot pass conclusive rules of evidence; that a legislative or administrative finding of public use is not conclusive on the courts and that, if the Legislature intended to deny to property owners the right to review a determination of the State Housing Commissioner, the law would be unconstitutional. However, the intention in the passage of this statute was to give the certificate great weight and to regard the matter therein certified as incontrovertible and conclusive in character, providing the certificate was issued in the manner prescribed by law and providing there was any basis for the determination of the commissioner, and the intention was also that the determination should be nullified [***3] only if palpably without reasonable foundation. The certificate may be issued only after a public hearing (Public Housing Law, § 134), notice of which must be published in the manner prescribed by law (§ 135). The statute when so construed is not unconstitutional.

2. In construing the meaning of the words "conclusive evidence", the presumption in favor of its constitutionality should be applied.

3. The fact that the project is sponsored by a trade union and that about 30% of the tenant-stockholders of the plaintiff corporation are members of that union or in some way connected with the garment trade does not justify a determination that the proposed taking is not for public use. It need not be shown that the development may be open for use by everybody in order to make it a public use. The taking of the property for a housing project may be for public use even though this apparent preference be granted provided the persons benefited are persons of low income (N. Y. Const., art. XVIII, § 1) and provided also that there is no discrimination because of race, creed, color or national origin (Public Housing Law, § 223). The main purpose of the legislation is to eliminate slum areas,  [***4] and if the public good is thus enhanced by the construction of the project it is unimportant that the corporation and its stockholders may ultimately reap a benefit.

4. Judgment is granted for the relief requested in petition.

 

2932 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Kaney v. New York State Civil Service Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Erie County


190 Misc. 944; 77 N.Y.S.2d 8; 1948 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2122



February 13, 1948 



DISPOSITION: For the foregoing reasons the petition should be dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, the New York State Civil Service Commission and others, filed a motion to dismiss petitioner applicants' action in which they sought an order prohibiting the Commission from taking any proceeding to cancel an examination taken by the applicants for the position of fire fighters in a certain city and the eligible list upon which the applicants were placed, pursuant to N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 11(7).


OVERVIEW: After the Commission conducted an investigation, it decided to prefer charges against the city's civil service commission and to seek a rescission of the examination and the eligible list and to cancel all appointments made therefrom. In dismissing the applicants' action, the court ruled that: (1) contrary to the applicants' claims, there was no factual allegation that supported an inference that the Commission members were biased or prejudiced or that they would not decide the matters in controversy fairly and impartially; (2) the Commission was not disqualified by reason of its preliminary investigation; (3) section 11(7) constitutionally gave the Commission the authority to invalidate examinations given by municipal commissions or to cancel eligible lists on the ground that the examination was not sufficiently practical in character and did not fairly test the relative capacity and fitness of the persons examined to discharge the duties of the position under N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 14; (3) the applicants were not entitled to notice of the Commission's hearing; and (4) the applicants did not have standing to maintain a prohibition action to enjoin the Commission's proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court granted the Commission's motion to dismiss.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- supervision by State of municipal civil service commission -- rescission of municipal eligible list -- (1) State Civil Service Commission not prohibited (Civ. Prac. Act, art. 78) from bringing proceeding for cancellation of examination, eligible list and appointments of petitioners as fire fighters of City of Lackawanna -- (2) matter not prejudged by State commission -- (3) State commission not disqualified by its preliminary investigation of city's commission -- (4) State commission has power to rescind eligible list and cancel appointments made therefrom, under Civil Service Law (§ 11, subd. 7), on ground that examination given not practical in character -- (5) subdivision 7 of section 11 of Civil Service Law not invasion of home rule provision of State Constitution or improper delegation of legislative power -- (6) no notice to petitioners required to be given by statute -- (7) section 22 of Civil Service Law, forbidding removal of veterans except for incompetency after hearing, inapplicable to  [***2] appointments void in first instance -- (8) petitioners without standing to maintain prohibition proceeding -- (9) since State commission's proceeding here not judicial or quasi-judicial, prohibition will not lie.

1. A petition in a proceeding under article 78 of the Civil Practice Act, in the nature of prohibition, to prohibit the State Civil Service Commission from taking any proceedings to cancel the examination taken by petitioners, the resulting eligible list and the appointments of petitioners as fire fighters in the fire department of the City of Lackawanna, which challenges a proceeding pending against such city's civil service commission before the State commission, on the ground that the State commission has prejudged the proceeding, that subdivision 7 of section 11 of the Civil Service Law (as amd. by L. 1944, ch. 435) under which the State commission has instituted the proceeding is unconstitutional and that the proceeding is invalid because petitioners have not been given any notice of the hearing and have not been made parties to the proceeding, must be dismissed for insufficiency.

2. The factual allegations in the petition and the exhibits show that the matter has [***3] not been prejudged but has been set down for hearing and if the hearing reveals that the charges are sustained, the State commission proposes to take appropriate action. The factual situation shown by the exhibits prevails over any conflicting allegations in the petition. The petition charges misconduct by employees of the State commission but contains no factual allegations to sustain an inference that the members of the commission are biased or prejudiced or that they will not decide the matters fairly.

3. The State commission is not disqualified by reason of its preliminary investigation. The commission has power to supervise and review the work of municipal commissions, and the statute (Civil Service Law, § 11, subd. 7) necessarily contemplates that the commission will conduct such preliminary ex parte investigations as it may deem proper. Before taking final action, the State commission must give the local commission an opportunity "to make a personal explanation and to file papers in opposition" to the action proposed to be taken, but the statute does not require that a judicial or quasi-judicial hearing precede the State commission's action. The function of the State [***4] commission is predominantly legislative or executive rather than judicial in character. Where the Legislature vests in a particular administrative agency the sole power of investigation and decision, the Legislature's purpose cannot be defeated by disqualification of the designated officer or agency on the ground of alleged prejudgment or bias.

4. Under subdivision 7 of section 11 of the Civil Service Law, as amended in 1944, the State commission has power to rescind an eligible list established by a municipal commission and cancel an appointment made from such rescinded list not only on the ground of fraud or material misstatement but also on the ground that "the provisions or purposes of this chapter are not properly or sufficiently carried out." This would seem to embrace the power to rescind lists and cancel appointments upon the ground that the examination given for the position was not sufficiently practical in character and did not fairly test the relative capacity and fitness of the persons examined to discharge the duties of the position within the standard of section 14 of the Civil Service Law. The charges served by the State commission upon the municipal commission indicate [***5] that the former intends to inquire whether the examinations were practical in character and complied with the standard established by section 14, whether the questions and answers were disclosed to certain candidates in advance of the examination and whether the oral examination was so poorly conducted that many of the candidates knew in advance the questions which were to be asked.

5. The 1944 amendment to subdivision 7 of section 11 of the Civil Service Law does not invade the home rule provisions of the State Constitution (art. IX, § 12) and is not an improper delegation of legislative power to an administrative agency. The maintenance and protection of the merit system in civil service is a matter of State concern and appropriate powers may be vested in the State commission in that regard by general law without invading the province of local government. The standard of the commission's action is sufficiently set forth in the statute so that no valid objection can be made that the Legislature has granted unfettered discretionary power to the commission.

6. The statute does not provide for notice to petitioners or anyone other than the local commission. Petitioners have no [***6] right to an administrative hearing in the absence of a provision therefor in the statute. If the commission issues an order canceling petitioners' appointments, they may seek relief in a proceeding under article 78 of the Civil Practice Act in the nature of mandamus.

7. Section 22 of the Civil Service Law which forbids the removal of veterans -- and petitioners are such -- except for incompetency or misconduct shown after hearing on due notice, is wholly inapplicable here. The question here is whether petitioners were legally appointed in the first instance and whether the eligible list from which they were appointed should be rescinded and the appointments cancelled ab initio. The protection against removal under section 22 attaches only after it is established that the veteran was lawfully appointed in the first place.

8. Petitioners have no standing to maintain a proceeding to prohibit the proceeding now pending before the State commission which proceeding will give the municipal commission an opportunity to make an explanation of the matters in controversy. Moreover, the hearing will embrace matters other than the examination in which petitioners are interested.

9. Prohibition [***7] will lie only to enjoin a judicial or quasi-judicial proceeding. Concededly the State commission has not instituted any quasi-judicial proceeding to which the petitioners are parties or by which they can be bound.

 

2933 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Beloff v. Consolidated Edison Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court, Special Term, New York County, Part III


81 N.Y.S.2d 440; 1948 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2810



February 2, 1948 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff shareholders' first cause of action against defendant utility company challenged its merger with a second utility company. The shareholders' second, third, and fourth causes of action were predicated upon acts of the utility company prior to the merger and sought an accounting of the utility company prior to the merger. The utility company filed a motion for summary judgment and a motion to dismiss the causes of action.


OVERVIEW: As to the first cause of action, the shareholders alleged that N.Y. Stock Corp. Law § 85 was unconstitutional and void insofar as it authorized this merger. The court disagreed and granted the utility company's motion for summary judgment. The Supreme Court of New York County had previously overruled the claim that the provision incorporated into § 85 permitting a stock corporation to merge with another corporation of similar power was unconstitutional. The court held that the matter was primarily one of public policy within the province of the legislature. Further, the remedy of appraisal and judgment was intended to afford fair and just compensation to dissenters. In the second, third, and fourth causes of action, the allegations of the first cause of action were repeated and the shareholders purported to bring suit both individually and as stockholders. The court held that the shareholders had no individual cause of action, as the alleged wrong was to the second utility company and no individual cause of action existed. Likewise, the shareholders could not bring suit derivatively because any wrong to the second utility company had vested in the utility company upon the merger.


OUTCOME: The court granted the utility company's motion for summary judgment dismissing the complaint as to the first cause of action. The court dismissed the complaint as to the second, third and fourth causes of action, with leave to serve an amended complaint within 20 days after service of a copy of the order. The court also held that there was no cause of action stated in favor of the shareholders and individuals.

 

2934 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Lemoyne Arms, Inc. v. Central New York Power Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, Onondaga County


191 Misc. 709; 76 N.Y.S.2d 703; 1948 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2103



January 31, 1948 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contractor filed suit against defendant utility company, seeking an order requiring the utility to continue to provide gas service to an apartment building. The intervening defendant was the Public Service Commission of the State of New York. Before the court was the Commission's motion for judgment and to dismiss the complaint on the ground that the court was without subject matter jurisdiction pursuant to N.Y. R. Civ. Prac. 107(2).


OVERVIEW: The complaint alleged that the utility company was the sole supplier to the public of Syracuse of electricity and gas for light, heat, and power. The contractor arranged for construction of several apartment houses to be heated by gas and advised the utility company of intention to construct the buildings with separate gas heating equipment. The contractor notified the utility company that such gas heating systems had been installed in several of the apartments and would shortly be installed in the remainder. The utility company laid pipes connecting from its gas mains in the adjacent streets into the basement of each of the apartments for servicing gas to such heating systems and to stoves and hot water heaters. The utility company then notified the contractor that it would discontinue all gas service to the apartments unless the gas heating units, which were in violation of restrictive regulations, were discontinued. The court held that there were no legal or statutory authority conferring sole authority on the Commission in an action such as the instant one. The court further held that there was a question of law presented in the complaint that required judicial determination.


OUTCOME: The court denied the Commission's motion for judgment and to dismiss the complaint.


HEADNOTES

Public utilities -- regulation by Public Service Commission -- (1) complaint, in action for injunction, alleges defendant, sole supplier in city of Syracuse of gas for light, heat and power, gave notice it would discontinue gas service to apartments unless gas heating discontinued, because installation of heating units violated restrictive regulations of Public Service Commission; that defendant obligated by franchise from city to furnish service; that plaintiff had no notice of proceeding involving use of gas for heating; Public Service Commission's motion for dismissal of complaint denied -- (2) question of law presented whether Legislature has power to deprive city and its citizens of benefits of franchise -- (3) Public Service Commission not clothed with sole jurisdiction as to use of gas -- (4) question of law presented as to whether notice to discontinue use of gas unreasonable and arbitrary -- (5) temporary injunction continued.

1. The complaint, in an action for an injunction, alleged that after plaintiff, which had constructed several apartments to be heated by gas, had installed gas heating [***2] systems and had paid defendant, sole supplier in the city of Syracuse of gas for light, heat, and power, for furnishing pipe and labor in connection with the laying of pipes from gas mains in the streets, and after meters had been installed in many of the apartments, defendant notified plaintiff that it would discontinue gas service within ten days unless the gas heating units were discontinued, because defendant had been informed that the heating units had been installed in violation of restrictive regulations of the Public Service Commission. Plaintiff was never given an opportunity to be heard in opposition to the commission's determination. It was further alleged that the city had granted a franchise to defendant's predecessor to lay pipes and mains in the streets, conditioned upon furnishing gas for cooking, hot water and space heating. A motion by the intervener, Public Service Commission, for a dismissal of the complaint on the ground that the court has no jurisdiction of the subject of the action is denied.

2. A question of law is presented as to whether, assuming the Legislature delegated sole authority to the commission to act on the questions arising between these parties,  [***3] the Legislature has power to deprive the city and its citizens of the benefits of a contract and franchise by which defendant is permitted to use the streets for its pipe lines. This question must be decided by the referee to whom the case has been assigned for determination.

3. The Public Service Commission is not clothed with sole jurisdiction to determine how the gas should be distributed.

4. Furthermore, a question of law is presented as to whether, under the circumstances, the notice given to abandon gas heating was unreasonable or arbitrary.

5. Since questions exist which permit the parties to be heard, the temporary injunction is continued.

 

2935 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Guaranty Trust Co. v. State


Claim No. 27969


Court of Claims of New York


191 Misc. 259; 76 N.Y.S.2d 824; 1948 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2113



January 29, 1948 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant, the Guaranty Trust Company of New York, filed suit against defendant, the State of New York, to recover moneys illegally paid into the Unemployment Insurance Fund. The court granted the State's motion to dismiss for noncompliance with § 10(4) of the N.Y. Court of Claims Act. The trust company appealed to the Appellate Division, Supreme Court, Third Department (New York), which reversed the order and remitted the matter to the court.


OVERVIEW: On appeal to the supreme court, the trust company had asserted a new theory and argued that its payments were enforced contributions, as distinguished from tax levies, that were used to augment the United States Government's Unemployment Trust Fund. It claimed further that a statutory trust resulted, that, when the express trust became invalid, the statutory trustee held the funds for the benefit of the settlor, that the statute of limitations did not run until after demand was made, and that its claim was, thus, timely filed. The State renewed its argument that the claim for the return of the illegal tax was not timely filed. The court regarded the law of the case as settled by the concluding sentence of the supreme court's opinion for reversal finding that there was a trust created by statute and that the public officials became trustees of the resultant trust when the enforced contributions involved were determined to be illegal. The court determined that the trust company was entitled to the claimed amount in addition to interest from the date that its application for a refund was finally denied when the appeal board affirmed the commissioner's ruling.


OUTCOME: The court awarded the trust company the amount claimed in addition to interest from the date its application for a refund of the amount was denied.


HEADNOTES

Unemployment insurance -- refund of contributions -- (1) reversal by Appellate Division made law of case that resultant trust created by enforced payment of sums into State Unemployment Insurance Fund, later held illegal, and that public officials were trustees thereof -- (2) interest of 4% on award granted from date of final denial of refund by appeal board, and not from date of payment.

1. Claimant State bank paid sums into the State Unemployment Insurance Fund for a period of time which, for that period, were subsequently held to be unconstitutional exactions. Where said bank's claim for refund was dismissed by the Court of Claims for failure to comply with subdivision 4 of section 10 of the Court of Claims Act [filing claim or notice of intention within six months of accrual], but on appeal, the Appellate Division reversed, the law of the case is settled that here a trust was created by statute and that the public officials became trustees of the resultant trust when the enforced contributions were determined to be illegal.

2. Claimant is entitled to interest on the award to be computed,  [***2] not from the date of payment, but from the date that its application for a refund was finally denied by the appeal board's affirmance of the commissioner's ruling. Moreover subdivision 6 of section 570 of the Labor Law provides that refunds shall be made without interest. Hence, had the commissioner directed a refund, claimant would have received no interest. Interest should be computed at the rate [4%] prescribed by section 16 of the State Finance Law.

 

2936 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Whitestone Boosters' Civic Ass'n


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


City Magistrate's Court of New York, Borough of Queens, Municipal Term


191 Misc. 121; 76 N.Y.S.2d 518; 1948 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2075



January 28, 1948 



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss on ground People have not made out a case beyond a reasonable doubt is denied and defendant corporation is found guilty as charged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with maintaining a bathing establishment in violation of New York City, N.Y., Sanitary Code § 340. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss on the ground that the premises were not used as a bathing establishment, that it came within an exception to § 340, and that § 340 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a membership corporation, leased a strip of shore front property and permitted use of the shorefront to its members and their guests for stipulated admission sums. Some 16,000 residents and property owners in the area were eligible for membership in defendant's corporation. The People charged defendant with maintaining a bathing establishment in violation of § 340 because the premises were not equipped with facilities and because the board of health issued no permit. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss, contending that the premises fell under an exception to § 340 because only defendant's stockholders used the shorefront. The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss and found it guilty. Although defendant was principally composed of members who were also stockholders, such individuals were not owners within the meaning of the exemption under § 340. Section 340 did not contemplate that 16,000 stockholders of a corporation owning a bathing establishment of small area were to be considered an exception to the general governing regulation. The menaces of pollution, tidal currents, and inadequate supervision were within the public health interest.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss and found defendant guilty as charged.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- maintenance of bathing establishment -- (1) section 340 of Sanitary Code excepts from regulations relating to facilities at bathing establishments "shore fronts * * * used only by the owner or his family"; shore front used by membership corporation whose members are stockholders in stock corporation owning property not excluded from such regulations; members not "owners"; membership corporation guilty of maintaining bathing establishment in violation of section 340 -- (2) provisions reasonable and constitute constitutional exercise of power to act where public health in jeopardy -- (3) contention that property not bathing establishment since required facilities not furnished, frivolous.

1. A membership corporation, lessee of shore front property, maintains a bathing establishment not equipped with facilities required by section 340 of the Sanitary Code of the City of New York and without [***2] a permit issued by the Board of Health. Less than 10% of approximately 16,000 residents and property owners in the area who are eligible for membership are members. The membership corporation is comprised principally of persons who are also stockholders in the landlord stock corporation. Section 340 defines a bathing establishment as not including "shore fronts * * * used only by the owner or his family". The word "owner" as used therein does not include members of the membership corporation. To include them in the word "owner" would encourage and permit a ruse of the law. The membership corporation is found guilty of maintaining a bathing establishment in violation of section 340.

2. Section 340 is a reasonable and constitutional exercise of power granted under section 558 of the New York City Charter to the Board of Health to act in cases where public health is in jeopardy.

3. A contention that the property is not a bathing establishment because the required facilities have not been provided, is frivolous.

 

2937 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Parkhill v. Todd Shipyards Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


190 Misc. 782; 76 N.Y.S.2d 363; 1948 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2062; 14 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P64,265



January 19, 1948 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employees brought an action against defendant employer for overtime compensation and penalties under the Fair Labor Standards Act of 1938, 29 U.S.C.S. § 201 et seq. The employer filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The employees formerly worked for the employer. Pursuant to a United States Supreme Court decision allowing compensation for walking and preparatory time, the employees brought an action for overtime compensation and penalties. The employer filed a motion to dismiss, and the court granted the motion because it no longer had jurisdiction over the action. The Portal-to-Portal Act of 1947 had been enacted and removed the court's jurisdiction under § 2(d). That subdivision applied retrospectively to all cases then pending. The retrospective provisions of the Act had always been held constitutional when challenged. Congress had the power to remove the jurisdiction of state courts to determine the rights of employees under a Federal statute.


OUTCOME: The court granted the employer's motion to dismiss with leave to the employees to file an amended complaint.


HEADNOTES

Master and servant -- Fair Labor Standards Act -- Portal-to-Portal Act of 1947 -- (1) complaint in action commenced prior to enactment of Federal Portal-to-Portal Act of 1947 for straight time and overtime for preliminary occupational activities, which does not allege that activities performed pursuant to contract or custom, required by such Act (§ 2, subd. [d]) as condition to court's jurisdiction, insufficient -- (2) Congress could withdraw rights created by Federal legislation -- (3) retroactive provisions in Portal-to-Portal Act constitutional.

1. The Federal Portal-to-Portal Act of 1947 (§ 2, subds. [a], [b], [d]), effective May 14, 1947, provides that no employer should be liable under the Federal Fair Labor Standards Act of 1938 for any activity engaged in prior to the enactment of the act, in an action commenced before or after the enactment of the act, except in an activity which was compensable under an express provision of a contract in effect at the time of such activity, or compensable under a custom in the place of employment in effect at the time of such activity. A complaint in an action commenced prior [***2] to May 14, 1947, seeking compensation, both straight time and overtime, for preliminary activities, such as walking, "shaping up", securing tools, changing clothes, etc., which does not allege that such activities were performed pursuant to any contract provision or custom or practice, is insufficient since such activities are not compensable under section 2 of the Portal-to-Portal Act, and the Supreme Court has no jurisdiction to entertain the action. The complaint is dismissed with leave to serve an amended complaint which will comply with such act.

2. In view of the findings of Congress and the express policy of the Portal-to-Portal Act, it was within the power of Congress to withdraw rights which were created by Federal legislation and certainly Congress could withdraw from State courts the power to enforce rights under a Federal statute.

3. The retroactive provisions of such act are constitutional. In the absence of any appellate court pronouncements to the contrary, and in view of the many precedents in other courts sustaining the constitutionality of the act, a court at nisi prius should not, unless the case is a clear one, declare an act of Congress unconstitutional.

 

2938 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Walk


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Surrogate's Court of New York, New York County


192 Misc. 237; 79 N.Y.S.2d 645; 1948 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2448



January 8, 1948 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant executors sought review of a pro forma taxing order for an estate that was entered by an appraiser (New York) at the instance of respondent state tax commission.


OVERVIEW: At the instance of the state tax commission, the appraiser entered a pro forma taxing order for an estate. On appeal, the executors contended that the inclusion in the gross estate of all the property in the decedent's record of ownership at his death was erroneous because it was in fact owned one half by his widow and was subject to a life estate in the other half for the benefit of the widow. The court held that: (1) N.Y. Tax Law § 249-r(5-a) stated that there was to be included in the gross estate property held as community property by a decedent and a surviving spouse under the law of any state, territory, or possession of the United States, or any foreign country; (2) the taxing statute in question was not unconstitutional as the executors contended; and (3) the meaning of the taxing statute was that a community property right created by private contract in a jurisdiction that permitted such creations of community interests was as much held "under the law" as it would be if the law itself created the right.


OUTCOME: The court entered an order confirming the tax imposed.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- estate tax -- community property -- (1) full value of property held by decedent in community with now surviving spouse, under agreement made in Belgium and permitted by Belgian law,  [***3] properly included in gross estate for tax purposes (Tax Law, § 249-r, subd. 5-a) -- (2) statutory direction for inclusion in gross estate of community property rights held "under the law" of foreign country includes rights created by contract under permissive statute -- (3) since similar Federal statute held constitutional, New York statute also constitutional -- (4) property also taxable under subdivision 3 of section 249-r since community property represents transfers made by decedent with intention that possession or enjoyment take effect on death.

1. Decedent and his widow, in 1895, prior to their marriage, entered into an agreement in Belgium providing that there should exist between them a "community of their property both personal and real, present and future * * * in accordance with article 1526 of the Civil Code." After providing for special treatment of certain tangibles it provided that as to the remaining property the survivor should have one half in full ownership and the other half for life. Subdivision 5-a of section 249-r of the Tax Law provides that there shall be included in the gross estate property "held as community property by the decedent and surviving [***4] spouse under the law of * * * any foreign country". The full value of property held by deceased in community with his now surviving widow was properly included in the gross estate for tax purposes.

2. Community property rights subject to tax comprise not only those which are themselves the creation of statute but those which are the creation of private agreement made under a permissive statute or case law. The meaning of subdivision 5-a of section 249-r is that a community property right created by private contract in a jurisdiction which permits such creations of community interests is as much held "under the law" as it would be if the law itself created the right.

3. The interpretation of our taxing statute will follow the interpretation given by the Supreme Court of the United States to like text in the Internal Revenue Code. The constitutionality of the like text in the Internal Revenue Code (§ 811, subd. [e], par. [2]) has been upheld and it follows that the New York statute is constitutional.

4. The effect of the agreement was that all property rights existent at the date of death in favor of the surviving spouse were transfers made with the intention of their taking [***5] effect in possession or enjoyment after death of the spouse first to die. In that concept the property is taxable under subdivision 3 of section 249-r of the Tax Law.

 

2939 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Holmes Electric Protective Co. v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Special Term, New York County


191 Misc. 378; 76 N.Y.S.2d 385; 1948 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 2064



January 7, 1948 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant comptroller, the city, and others, sought dismissal of plaintiff taxpayer's action seeking a declaratory judgment that a utility tax did not apply to the taxpayer, and to recover sums paid under protest.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer owned and operated a security business that included the use of electrical alarms. A utility tax was assessed by the city. Defendants contended that the taxpayer's action for declaratory relief should be dismissed because the taxpayer's exclusive remedy was administrative per New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code §§ Q41-6.0, Q41-7.0, and Q41-9.0. The court did not rule on the merits of the taxpayer's claims that the tax either did not apply or was unconstitutional. However, the court denied the motion to dismiss because the taxpayer's complaint contained allegations sufficient to present a genuine question which required a declaration of the rights of the parties with respect to applicability or unconstitutionality of the tax.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' motion to dismiss.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- municipal utility taxes -- (1) complaint alleges plaintiff is engaged in protecting customers' premises against burglary and that comptroller of city of New York had served notice of deficiency under utility tax laws based on receipts from customers; complaint states cause of action for declaratory judgment where it alleges plaintiff is not furnishing telegraphic service and seeks refund of taxes paid under protest -- (2) "exclusive remedies" provision in utility tax laws no bar to plaintiff's action which states inapplicability of laws to it -- (3) determination whether plaintiff's assertion of inapplicability is correct not necessary on defendant's motion to dismiss complaint.

1. Plaintiff, a company engaged in the business of protecting the premises of its customers against burglary and unauthorized entry, states a cause of action for a declaratory judgment in its complaint where it alleges that the comptroller of the city of New York had served on plaintiff a notice of deficiency under the utility tax laws of said city for the period from May 1, 1942, to December 31, 1943, based on plaintiff's receipts from its customers;  [***2] that the assessment was made against plaintiff as a "utility" or "vendor of utility services" and as a person selling telegraphy or furnishing telegraph services; that the assessment was made pursuant to Local Laws of the City of New York, No. 49 of 1941, No. 29 of 1942, and No. 22 of 1943; that plaintiff was not engaged in the business of selling or furnishing telegraphic service and accordingly the utility tax is not applicable to plaintiff; that plaintiff had paid, under protest, additional utility taxes for the period from July, 1938, to April, 1942, and plaintiff seeks recovery of the amount of such payment after defendant's refusal to refund.

2. The "exclusive remedies" provisions in the city's utility tax laws which defendant claims accords the comptroller, in the first instance, jurisdiction to decide the issues presented in the complaint are not a bar to plaintiff's action. Declaratory judgment actions and other available remedies are permitted where the tax laws are inapplicable to a taxpayer or where they are unconstitutional in their application.

3. On this motion to dismiss the complaint on the ground that the court does not have jurisdiction of the subject of the action,  [***3] the court does not have to determine whether plaintiff's assertions of inapplicability or unconstitutionality are correct. It is sufficient upon this motion that there be a showing that a genuine question is presented which requires a declaration of the rights of the parties with respect to applicability or unconstitutionality. Whether the amendments to the utility tax laws, made after plaintiff was successful in sustaining its claims to inapplicability (Matter of Holmes Elec. Protective Co. v. McGoldrick, 262 App. Div. 514, 30 N.Y.S.2d 589, affd. 288 N. Y. 635, 42 N.E.2d 737), brought plaintiff within the sphere of the taxing statute is a matter for final determination in this action.
